Updated and edited review: Customer service in the service department can be bad. (My story below.) If you want service work done in Simi... you may want to consider one of the other options in town.

I've bought high end gloves and occasional parts here. Very large selection of bikes, great selection of gloves during the summer, smaller selection in the winter. Good selection of other gear.  Some of their sales people seem pretty cool, although I've never actually shopped for a motorcycle here.

My last experience here is the last time I'll go here for service at least, maybe last time ever.  (I MIGHT still check this place out when shopping for bikes, because their selection is seriously impressive.) I took a wheel and tire in to get mounted. A day and a half later, I still hadn't heard from them.  I called to find out what was taking so ridiculously long. Turns out they had just "forgotten" to call me to let me know it was done. I went in to pick it up, and they charged me twice what it should have cost. I commented on the insane price--the person checking me out still didn't realize there was a problem.  I thought I'd just gotten screwed, paid my bill and left, never to return.  After leaving a scathing review here, they called me, apologized claiming it was a mistake, and refunded half of my money. This brought the cost down to a reasonable $25 (approx. w/ tax and disposal fee).  Was it an unforgivable mistake?  No, but why bother going back here when there are so many other shops that have treated me quite well? <Resp>None< /Resp>< Text>
SVC is by far the worst motorcycle dealer in Ventura County, if not all of Southern California.  Their parts department does not carry a large inventory insuring that their customers will have to wait.  Their service department is staffed by young, untrained technicians who perform shoddy work.

I purchased a motorcycle from them in 2001.  Two years later it developed an intermittent missing problem and I brought it to them under warranty.  They tried on three separate occasions to find and repair the problem and couldn't.  They ended up giving the bike back to me un-repaired.  I then brought the bike to a competing dealer who diagnosed and located the problem in 10 minutes, ordered the part and returned my motorcycle in three days.

While SVC had my motorcycle the last time under warranty, they kept it for 4 weeks, broke my carburetor float bowls, glued them back together with epoxy, replaced defective parts with used ones, stored it outside in the rain (customary for them) and they returned the motorcycle to me completely filthy and corroded.  They refused to repair the damage they had caused or even detail the bike.

I highly recommend that you avoid Simi Valley Cycles.</Text>

< Text>
Last visit, my fiancee and I took a friend from out of town to Pedro's. The friendly woman at the counter suggested we try the Molcajete for four. The Molcajete sits in a volcanic bowl that is a bubbling aromatic mass of carne asada, chicken and pork, carrots, radishes, serrano peppers, onion, and topped with sliced avocado and cheese, and grilled shrimp. It was phenomenal. It's almost like stewed meat, but spicier and more meaty. My friend from out of town was so impressed. It was the first time he's ever been to Dixon. Our meal for the three of us, including sodas, totaled 26$ and we had leftovers to spare! Would totally be down to go 2-3 more times before Xmas break ends üëå< /Text>

Okay.... I consider myself a bit of a Mexican cuisine fanatic/connoisseur. We were in Dixon, CA (we certainly don‚Äôt come to Dixon much) but had to pick up furniture. We were hungry and turned to Yelp to find somewhere local with good reviews.

At first we thought the directions were a mistake. It‚Äôs adjoining to a food mart/gas station building. Apprehensive my husband got out to inspect the restaurant. He quickly waved us in...

Pedro is who greeted us. Such a nice man. He was engaging with our son & helped us order. I got El Pastor tacos & Carnitas. He brought out things for us to sample like pickled onions with pineapple. Needless to say these were the best tacos I‚Äôve ever had (yes ever).

My husband went with Pedro‚Äôs recommendation and had Sandwich full of marinated meat, veggies and avocado. (I can‚Äôt remember the name).
We were stuffed and enjoyed the food so much I purchased some El Pastor & Carnitas to take home.

Turns out Pedro is a fixture in Dixon and has a following of loyal customers. This is where the locals go for amazing Mexican food. We got Pedro‚Äôs card and he does event cratering too.

We we‚Äôll definitely go out of our way to eat here and refer our friends.</Text>

< Review>
After my regular nail tech cancelled on me last minute, I Google searched for other shops as I was attending a special event and needed nails and pedi ASAP. This place is not too far from the preserves and right off the 60 fwy Euclid Ave. exit. They accept walk-ins and although I arrived 15 minutes after their 9:30am open time, the place was packed! I waited about 10-15 minutes and got a full set and spa pedi.

Pros: Fast, clean, professional, takes walk-ins, no children allowed unless they are getting services done on them (makes for a quiet, true spa experience)

Cons: Cash tip only, pricey, and for those with small children, they aren't allowed to maintain a spa atmosphere (yes, I do have children, but for me it's a PRO as it gives me an excuse to pamper myself alone) there are plenty of nail salons that allow children

I enjoyed my time there and I'll be back again!< /Review>

<text>Interesting and disappointing experience at Photoworks.  My wife and I accompanied my daughter to Photoworks to drop off her 35mm film and noticed two framed black and white photographs on the wall, one depicting a smiling Asian couple holding hands while walking and the other depicting an African American male violently striking an African American young lady in the face! See attached photo for context.

My wife pointed these two dramatically contrasting framed photos to me and we immediately addressed our alarm and concerns to the first available store representative. To our surprise, store representative said she had nothing to do with the selection and display of the photos. We then asked three staff members  for the manager on duty and one of the staff members stated he was the owner, so we addressed our concerns with him about the juxtaposition of the two photos and the violent stereotypical message reinforcing African American male violence and domestic violence.

The owner said he was just made aware of the frame photos on the wall 5 minutes ago (4 minutes too late in my opinion) and the photos were left over from an exhibit and he would immediately remedy the situation by removing the offensive photo from the wall.

We left Photoworks with the assurance the offensive black and white frame photo would be removed from the wall and hopefully from their store.

My daughter who just completed her freshman year at the local university with a 3.5 GPA was disturbed and surprised about our experience as she has had good experiences at Photoworks. As a result, I am giving this location 2 stars.

<user_name>diana turner< /user_name><date>1580424477982</date>< rating>
1</rating>
< review>
I have been using this lab for over two years, having processed over thirty rolls of film with them.  I do BW film almost exclusively, usually Kodak tri-x.  First the good.  The development and scanning has been good and the negatives come back clean. Now for the bad. I sent in two rolls which they processed and returned with CD of scans and the CD was blank.  On another occasion I sent them two rolls which were processed and scanned to CD but they sent someone else's film back with their scans on the CD and my film also went to some other person.  Depending on how busy they are turnaround can be up to two weeks despite my using UPS and Fedex for mailing.  They eventually get it right but I would say customer service is poor and a hassle and they don't take time to listen to complaints but just cut any phone conversation short.  I am seriously thinking of giving up on my love for BW film and going back to digital.  It just isn't worth it.
Follow up to above review.  After sending my film to another customer they finally retrieved it.  When I talked to them they said they would rescan it to CD and send it by overnight mail.  Well they didn't send it by overnight and I finally received the roll three weeks after sending it in.  The film negatives were not cut and mounted in archival sleeves.  Moreover the scans were standard jpeg and not the deluxe jpg I had ordered.  I called them and told them I wanted a full refund and would not do business with them again.< /review>

< user>
113746935163628696237</user>
< review>
I've likely spent $8,000+ dollars here with both personal and client work (commercial and editorial) throughout the last 4-5 years. Maybe even more than that but wanted to stay on the generous side for this review.

I'm generally happy with the convenience factor but if you are a professional/trained artist or knowledgeable/experienced, you'll see the corners that are cut and the inconsistencies throughout their post-processing (even though the cost is at a premium and continually rising).

For instance, if you ask for wide-channel scanning when you drop-off, they will slap black boarders around your images after the scan rather than actually doing it while scanning the negative or simply forgot to do it all together. In some cases, they will say it can't be done because they've cut the film already (which behooves me as I get cut 6 so shouldn't the majority of the images still be wide-channel scannable?).  A las, one must call them up, listen to a bit of their whining about having to re-scan and then half the time it's the same result ‚Äì black frames slapped. In a few cases they have taken creative liberties by cropping the image slightly slapping on the boarder (even worse than before). So as an entire week goes by, I pick up my negatives and end up scanning them myself at home (no refund of course) and capture the beautiful Hasselblad notches in every frame.</review>
